Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

    Inlining exceptional tail calls is currently broken, as we return



<span class="line"><!---->    Inlining exceptional tail calls is currently broken, as we return<!----></span>



<br>





    immediately after the inlined call instead of redirecting to the handler



<span class="line"><!---->    immediately after the inlined call instead of redirecting to the handler<!----></span>



<br>

<br>





    



<span class="line"><!---->    <!----></span>



<br>

<span class="line"><!---->    This CL fixes this by adding IfException and IfSuccess projections to<!----></span>

    the call node we generate for the tail call from the callee, if the call

<span class="line"><!---->Please note that, based on my investigation, I believe that this does not require an experimental flag to trigger. However, it is difficult for me to directly remove the code related to wasm GC due to the limited modifiability of the wasm's POC. <!----></span>



<br>





Therefore, it is highly likely that it complies with the requirements for V8 rewards. 



<span class="line"><!---->Therefore, it is highly likely that it complies with the requirements for V8 rewards. <!----></span>

[wasm] Fix control input for projections when inlining



<span class="line"><!---->[wasm] Fix control input for projections when inlining<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





When inlining a tail call with multi-return into a call, we generate



<span class="line"><!---->When inlining a tail call with multi-return into a call, we generate<!----></span>



<br>





projections for its outputs. Those projections should take as control



<span class="line"><!---->projections for its outputs. Those projections should take as control<!----></span>



<br>





input the IfSuccess node rather than the call itself.



<span class="line"><!---->input the IfSuccess node rather than the call itself.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

Thanks for the report! We currently don't believe that this issue has any security implications as control inputs to Projections aren't used by the compiler in any interesting way, so we're treating this as Type-Bug. However, do let us know if you believe that this issue can in fact be exploited!



<span class="line"><!---->Thanks for the report! We currently don't believe that this issue has any security implications as control inputs to Projections aren't used by the compiler in any interesting way, so we're treating this as Type-Bug. However, do let us know if you believe that this issue can in fact be exploited!<!----></span>

<br>





    [wasm] Fix inlining of tail calls in a try block



<span class="line"><!---->    [wasm] Fix inlining of tail calls in a try block<!----></span>



<br>





    



<span class="line"><!---->    <!----></span>



<br>





    Inlining exceptional tail calls is currently broken, as we return



<span class="line"><!---->    Inlining exceptional tail calls is currently broken, as we return<!----></span>



<br>





    immediately after the inlined call instead of redirecting to the handler



<span class="line"><!---->    immediately after the inlined call instead of redirecting to the handler<!----></span>



<br>





    in case of an exception.



<span class="line"><!---->    in case of an exception.<!----></span>



<br>





    



<span class="line"><!---->    <!----></span>



<br>





    This was reproduced by executing the "mjsunit/wasm/return-calls-eh" test



<span class="line"><!---->    This was reproduced by executing the "mjsunit/wasm/return-calls-eh" test<!----></span>



<br>





    with --exceptional-wasm-inlining enabled.



<span class="line"><!---->    with --exceptional-wasm-inlining enabled.<!----></span>



<br>





    



<span class="line"><!---->    <!----></span>



<br>





    This CL fixes this by adding IfException and IfSuccess projections to



<span class="line"><!---->    This CL fixes this by adding IfException and IfSuccess projections to<!----></span>



<br>





    the call node we generate for the tail call from the callee, if the call



<span class="line"><!---->    the call node we generate for the tail call from the callee, if the call<!----></span>



<br>





    itself had exception handling.



<span class="line"><!---->    itself had exception handling.<!----></span>



<br>





    



<span class="line"><!---->    <!----></span>



<br>





    R=



<span class="line"><!---->    R=<!----></span>

          border: var(--chops-accessible-border);
          z-index: 999;
          box-shadow: 2px 3px 8px 0px hsla(0, 0%, 0%, 0.3);
          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;

           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container td {
          padding: 0.25em 8px;
          white-space: nowrap;
        }
        .screenreader-hidden {
          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;
          width: 1px;
        }
      </style>
